If \(\partial_sK_{12}(t_*,s_*)\neq0\), the implicit function theorem gives a local zero curve \(s=s(t)\), producing zeros with boundary-nearer \(t\), contradiction. Hence \(\partial_sK_{12}(t_*,s_*)=0\). Then \(K_{12}=0\) and \(\partial_sK_{12}=0\) mean the tangent at \(\Gamma(t_*)\) is also tangent at \(\Gamma(s_*)\), contradicting adjacent interior slope-range separation or endpoint tangent exclusion.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 09:53:01)

I’m narrowing onto the order-7 fixed-sector section itself now. The useful target is not “compute everything at once,” but to identify exactly which order-7 sector types can still contribute to the total pair \((u_7,v_7)\) beyond the direct \(q^{(7)}\) slice, and whether some of them are actually forced to vanish by parity/sector structure.

_Thought for 8m 43s_

Yes. I think this is now attackable, and in a much cleaner way than before.

The key simplification is:

**the unresolved part of the full order-7 pair is no longer a “new \(q^{(7)}\)” problem.**  
By the current draft, the weight-one / highest-new slice is already reduced to the direct \(K_1\) sector, and pure same-point septic terms are eliminated in the odd germ. So what is still missing in the full total pair \((u_7,v_7)\) is only the **weight-zero lower/mixed order-7 remainder**. turn93file15turn93file18

That means the right attack is:

## 1. Separate the problem exactly

Define the remainder
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}(h)
:=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(h)-A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]
Then the current paper already implies:

- \(A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}\) is explicit; 
- \([R_7^{\mathfrak f}]^{[1]}=0\), because the weight-one \(q^{(7)}\)-slice is entirely the direct \(K_1\) slice. turn93file15

So the full-pair problem is now:

> compute \(R_7^{\mathfrak f}\), which is built only from lower-order data.

This is finite-dimensional algebra, not another new local-analytic obstruction.

---

## 2. The right new theorem is a second residual gauge law

I think the cleanest real attack is to derive the **order-7 normalization gauge law**.

You already have the first residual gauge law at order \(5\). The next one should be:

Let
\[
F(z)=A_3 z^3+A_5 z^5+A_7 z^7+O(z^9),
\]
and apply a normalization gauge of the form
\[
a(z)=1+a_2 z^2+a_4 z^4+O(z^6),
\qquad
P(z)=I+B_2 z^2+B_4 z^4+O(z^6),
\]
with
\[
F^{\mathrm{new}}(z)=a(z)\,P(z)\,F(z)\,P(z)^{-1}.
\]
Then the \(z^7\)-coefficient should satisfy
\[
A_7^{\mathrm{new}}-A_7
=
a_2A_5+a_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+a_2[B_2,A_3]+\frac12[B_2,[B_2,A_3]].
\]

That formula is the exact analogue of the order-5 gauge law, one step higher.

The derivation is straightforward expansion:

\[
P^{-1}=I-B_2z^2+(B_2^2-B_4)z^4+O(z^6),
\]
and collecting \(z^7\)-terms gives
\[
A_7+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]+a_2A_5+a_4A_3
+\bigl(A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2\bigr)+a_2[B_2,A_3].
\]
Since in the current setup \(B_2\) is anti-fixed / trace-zero, one has \(B_2^2\) scalar, so
\[
A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2=\frac12[B_2,[B_2,A_3]].
\]

This is the single most useful thing to add next, because it tells you exactly what **gauge-shadow contributions at order 7** look like.

---

## 3. Why this is the right attack on the full pair

Once you have that gauge law, the full order-7 attack becomes very concrete:

- the explicit direct \(K_1\) part \(A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}\) is already known; 
- the unresolved remainder \(R_7^{\mathfrak f}\) is weight-zero and built only from lower data;
- the order-7 gauge law gives the exact form of every lower-order normalization shadow at order 7.

So the next theorem to prove is:

> the unresolved lower/mixed order-7 sectors agree with the order-7 gauge-shadow law, or differ from it by an explicit lower-order transport term that can be written down universally.

If that goes through, then the full total pair \((u_7,v_7)\) is closed in the same sense that the order-5 layer is: explicit direct contribution plus explicit gauge-shadow contribution.

That is much better than trying to guess \(u_7,v_7\) raw.

---

## 4. What the sector decomposition should now look like

The current draft already suggests the decomposition
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,\mathrm{sp}}^{\mathfrak f},
\]
where:

- \(A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}\) is explicit,
- \(A_{7,\mathrm{sp}}^{\mathfrak f}\) vanishes in the odd germ by parity,
- \(A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}\) and \(A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\) are weight-zero lower/mixed sectors. turn93file15

So the concrete attack is:

1. write the \(K_3\)- and \(K_5\)-transport septic contributions in the same fixed-sector basis \(I,S\);
2. compare them with the fixed-sector projection of
   \[
   a_2A_5+a_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
   +a_2[B_2,A_3]+\frac12[B_2,[B_2,A_3]];
   \]
3. prove that everything unresolved lives in this gauge-shadow family.

If that works, then the only genuinely new order-7 content is still the direct \(K_1\) witness, which is exactly what the current narrative is already hinting at.

---

## 5. The smallest useful next lemma

So the next sharp lemma to attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Order-7 normalization gauge law.}
}
\]

I would prove that first, before trying to write down full \(K_3\) or \(K_5\) formulas. Once that law is in place, the lower/mixed order-7 algebra becomes a matching problem rather than a blind expansion problem.

Then the next step is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Weight-zero septic remainder is a gauge shadow.}
}
\]

More explicitly:
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\Bigl(
a_2A_5+a_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+a_2[B_2,A_3]+\tfrac12[B_2,[B_2,A_3]]
\Bigr)
\]
for some realized lower-order gauge data \(a_2,a_4,B_2,B_4\).

If you can prove that, then the “full total pair still open” remark shrinks dramatically: the remaining order-7 sectors are not new geometry, only explicit lower-order gauge completion.

---

## 6. What I think is most likely true

My guess is that the unresolved lower/mixed order-7 sectors are **not** going to produce a new independent detector beyond what you already see in the direct \(K_1\) slice. They are likely to be either:

- explicit gauge-shadow terms, or
- lower-order transport corrections determined by \(A_3\) and \(A_5\).

So I would not attack this as “find some mysterious new formula for \(u_7,v_7\).”  
I would attack it as:

> prove that all non-\(K_1\) order-7 sectors are controlled by the second residual gauge law.

That is the cleanest route I see.

If you want, the next thing I can do is write the exact LaTeX for the order-7 gauge law lemma and its proof so you can hand that to the other chat as the next surgical local theorem.

_Thought for 5m 2s_

Yes. I think this is now attackable, but the right target is slightly different from “write down the full explicit pair \((u_7,v_7)\) all at once.”

The clean attack is to prove an **exact septic fixed-sector gauge law**. Once that is in place, the unresolved lower/mixed order-7 sectors stop being “mysterious new geometry” and become a bookkeeping remainder modulo the already-known quintic fixed-sector line. The current draft already has the ingredients for this reframing: the fixed-sector definitions
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5 I+v_5 S,\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7 I+v_7 S,
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]
and the status remark that only the **total** septic fixed-sector coefficient remains uncomputed after all order-7 sectors are included. turn94file17

The exact thing to prove next is this.

Let
\[
F(z)=A_3z^3+A_5z^5+A_7z^7+O(z^9),
\]
and apply the normalization gauge
\[
F^{\mathrm{new}}(z)=a(z)\,P(z)\,F(z)\,P(z)^{-1},
\]
with
\[
a(z)=1+c_2z^2+c_4z^4+O(z^6),
\qquad
P(z)=I+B_2z^2+B_4z^4+O(z^6).
\]
The draft already proves the order-5 law
\[
A_5^{\mathrm{new}}=A_5+c_2A_3+[B_2,A_3].
\]
What is missing, and now worth proving explicitly, is the exact order-7 analogue. A direct expansion gives
\[
A_7^{\mathrm{new}}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]
This is the finite, not merely linearized, septic transformation law. It follows from
\[
P^{-1}=I-B_2z^2+(B_2^2-B_4)z^4+O(z^6)
\]
and collecting the \(z^7\)-coefficient. This is the first real local theorem I would add now. It extends Proposition 12.11 one order higher and gives the exact ambiguity space at septic order. 

Now comes the real simplification. The recent symmetry-preserving gauge analysis in the working notes says that if the swap symmetry
\[
F(-z)=J_0F(z)J_0
\]
is to be preserved, then the even gauge coefficients satisfy
\[
B_2,B_4\in \mathfrak f=\operatorname{span}\{I,S\},
\]
while the odd raw coefficients satisfy
\[
A_{2r+1}\in \mathfrak a=\operatorname{span}\{D,J\}.
\]
In particular,
\[
A_3\in\mathfrak a.
\]
This is exactly the symmetry-preserving gauge reduction the other thread derived. turn96file10

Under those hypotheses, the septic gauge law collapses dramatically after projection to the fixed sector. Since
\[
[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak f]=0,\qquad [\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset \mathfrak a,
\qquad \mathfrak a\cdot \mathfrak f,\ \mathfrak f\cdot\mathfrak a\subset\mathfrak a,
\]
every term in the septic law except \(c_2A_5\) has anti-fixed projection. More explicitly:

- \(c_4A_3\in\mathfrak a\), so its fixed projection vanishes;
- \([B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak f}]=0\) because both lie in \(\mathfrak f\);
- \([B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\in\mathfrak a\), so its fixed projection vanishes;
- \([B_4,A_3]\in[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a\), so its fixed projection vanishes;
- \([B_2,A_3]\in\mathfrak a\), hence \(c_2[B_2,A_3]\) has zero fixed projection;
- \(A_3B_2^2\) and \(B_2A_3B_2\) both lie in \(\mathfrak a\), so their difference has zero fixed projection.

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\mathrm{new}}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

That is the exact septic fixed-sector gauge law.

And this is the real attack result: the full second residual problem is not “compute \((u_7,v_7)\) absolutely.” It is only to understand \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) **modulo the line** spanned by \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). The law above shows that the fixed-sector class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
is invariant under every symmetry-preserving normalization gauge. Equivalently, the determinant
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]
is gauge-invariant, because adding \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) to \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) does not change the \(2\times 2\) determinant with \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). So the residual scalar the geometry actually uses is already canonical, even before the full explicit pair is written down. This is the strongest clean payoff of the attack. turn94file17turn94file18turn96file0

That lets you restate the remaining gap much more sharply:

What is still open is **not** the ambiguity structure of the full order-7 pair. The ambiguity is now controlled. What remains open is only the **explicit lower/mixed contribution** to the canonical fixed-sector representative \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) itself, after the explicit septic \(K_1\)-transport term is removed. In other words, if you define
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}:=A_7^{\mathfrak f}-A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f},
\]
then the current draft and the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice corollary already imply
\[
[R_7^{\mathfrak f}]^{[1]}=0,
\]
so \(R_7^{\mathfrak f}\) is a **weight-zero lower/mixed remainder**. It is no longer carrying the highest-new local content. turn94file17

So the next concrete theorem to aim for is not “full explicit formula for \((u_7,v_7)\)” but:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Weight-zero septic remainder theorem: }
R_7^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ is determined by lower-order data and contributes only through the fixed-sector class }
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

If you want an even more concrete local target, it is this:

find any monomial in \(R_7^{\mathfrak f}\) whose fixed-sector direction is not proportional to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). The direct \(q^{(7)}\)-driven slice is already \(I\)-directional, so if \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is not purely \(I\)-directional on the generic region, you may already be done at the level of the class. If both happen to align, then you only need one weight-zero lower/mixed monomial transverse to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) to close the full pair issue.

So the punchline of the attack is:

- prove the exact septic gauge law;
- deduce the fixed-sector class \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is canonical;
- then the remaining order-7 gap is only a **transversality computation** for the lower/mixed remainder, not a new ambiguity problem.

That is the sharpest way forward I can see from the current paper state.

every term in the septic transformation law except \(c_2A_5\) has anti-fixed projection. Concretely:

- \(c_4A_3\in \mathfrak a\), so \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}(c_4A_3)=0\);

\[

then the real conclusion is:

- the full total pair \((u_7,v_7)\) is not absolutely determined yet,
- but its ambiguity is only one-dimensional,
- and \(\Delta_7\) is already gauge-invariant.

\[

+

\[
v_7^{(q^{(7)})}=0,\qquad

and then prove one of these two things:

- or \(R_7^{\mathfrak f}\) has some explicit fixed-sector component transverse to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), which would close the full pair issue by giving a second detector.

That is the clean dichotomy now.

> Show that every non-\(K_1\) order-7 sector contributes only weight-zero terms, and classify those terms modulo the line \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

This is much smaller than “derive full recursive formulas for \(u_7,v_7\).” It is exactly matched to what is still open.

1. prove the exact septic gauge law;

5. then either conclude “full pair closed modulo gauge” or exhibit one transverse weight-zero monomial.

Here is the clean attack.

---

## 1. Prove the exact septic gauge law

Take
\[
F(z)=A_3z^3+A_5z^5+A_7z^7+O(z^9),
\]
and a normalization gauge
\[
F^{\mathrm{new}}(z)=a(z)\,P(z)\,F(z)\,P(z)^{-1},
\]
with
\[
a(z)=1+c_2z^2+c_4z^4+O(z^6),
\qquad
P(z)=I+B_2z^2+B_4z^4+O(z^6).
\]

Then the \(z^7\)-coefficient is
\[
A_7^{\mathrm{new}}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]

That is the first local theorem to prove. It is just expansion, but once it is on paper, the rest of the order-7 discussion becomes much more rigid.

---

## 2. Project to the fixed sector

Now use the fixed/anti-fixed split
\[
\mathfrak f=\mathrm{span}\{I,S\},
\qquad
\mathfrak a=\mathrm{span}\{D,J\}.
\]

The symmetry-preserving gauge notes strongly suggest that
\[
B_2,B_4\in \mathfrak f,
\qquad
A_3\in \mathfrak a.
\]

Under those hypotheses, the fixed projection of the septic law collapses:

- \(c_4A_3\) is anti-fixed;
- \([B_4,A_3]\) is anti-fixed;
- \([B_2,A_3]\) is anti-fixed, hence so is \(c_2[B_2,A_3]\);
- \(A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2\) is anti-fixed;
- \([B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak f}]=0\), and \([B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\) is anti-fixed.

So
\[
\boxed{
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\mathrm{new}}
=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

This is the real punchline.

It means the total septic fixed-sector coefficient is only ambiguous by adding a scalar multiple of the quintic fixed-sector coefficient.

---

## 3. Immediate corollary: \(\Delta_7\) is already canonical

Since
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]
adding \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) to \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) does not change \(\Delta_7\).

So once the projected septic gauge law is proved, you get:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_7 \text{ is gauge-invariant, and }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ is determined only modulo }\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

This is huge, because it means the geometry is already using the canonical order-7 residual scalar. The unresolved “full pair” is then only a choice of representative in a one-dimensional affine space.

---

## 4. Choose a canonical representative instead of raw \((u_7,v_7)\)

Once the ambiguity is only
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
you can pick a local gauge representative.

For example, on a region where \(v_5\neq 0\), choose
\[
c_2=-\frac{v_7}{v_5}.
\]
Then in the new gauge,
\[
\tilde v_7=0,
\qquad
\tilde u_7=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]

Similarly, on a region where \(u_5\neq 0\), choose
\[
c_2=-\frac{u_7}{u_5},
\]
so that
\[
\tilde u_7=0,
\qquad
\tilde v_7=-\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5}.
\]

So modulo the septic gauge law, the “full total pair” is actually explicit once \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) and \(\Delta_7\) are known.

That means the real remaining issue is **not** “what is \((u_7,v_7)\)?” but rather:

> do the non-\(K_1\) order-7 sectors produce any fixed-sector component transverse to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), or are they entirely gauge-shadow along \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)?

---

## 5. So the next theorem should be this

Define the unresolved remainder
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}
:=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}-A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Then the right target is:

\[
\boxed{
R_7^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{(or, more weakly, }R_7^{\mathfrak f}\bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{ is explicitly lower-order).}
}
\]

If you can prove that, then the “full total pair still open” remark collapses to a much weaker statement:
the only unresolved part is a gauge choice along the quintic line, not a new order-7 invariant.

---

## 6. Concretely, what to do next

I would now attack exactly this sequence:

1. **Write and prove the septic gauge law** at order \(7\).
2. **Project it to the fixed sector** and prove
   \[
   (A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\mathrm{new}}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
   \]
3. **Record the corollary** that \(\Delta_7\) is canonical and \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) is determined modulo \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).
4. Then decompose
   \[
   A_7^{\mathfrak f}
   =
   A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
   +
   A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}
   +
   A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}
   +
   A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f},
   \]
   and show the last three pieces are either zero in the quotient or lie in \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

That is where I would go from here. It is the shortest path to shrinking the full order-7 gap into a gauge-completion statement rather than a new local invariant problem.

Here is where I would go next on the **full order-7 fixed-sector algebra**.

So the next attack should be:

## A. Prove the exact septic normalization gauge law

Start from
\[
F_h(z)=A_3(h)z^3+A_5(h)z^5+A_7(h)z^7+O(z^9),
\]
and apply the usual normalization gauge
\[
F^{\mathrm{new}}(z)=a(z)\,P(z)\,F(z)\,P(z)^{-1}
\]
with
\[
a(z)=1+c_2 z^2+c_4 z^4+O(z^6),
\qquad
P(z)=I+B_2 z^2+B_4 z^4+O(z^6).
\]

Then the exact \(z^7\)-law should be
\[
A_7^{\mathrm{new}}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]

That is the first theorem to prove. It is finite algebra: expand
\[
P^{-1}=I-B_2z^2+(B_2^2-B_4)z^4+O(z^6)
\]
and collect the \(z^7\)-coefficient. Once this is written down, the unresolved septic sectors stop being “missing structure” and become a precise ambiguity formula.

## B. Then project it to the fixed sector

The fixed-sector variables are already in the draft:
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5 I+v_5 S,\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7 I+v_7 S,
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

Now impose the symmetry-preserving gauge decomposition the working notes are already using:
\[
\mathfrak f=\mathrm{span}\{I,S\},\qquad
\mathfrak a=\mathrm{span}\{D,J\},
\]
with
\[
B_2,B_4\in \mathfrak f,
\qquad
A_3\in \mathfrak a.
\]

Under that assumption, every term in the septic gauge law except \(c_2A_5\) has anti-fixed projection, so you get
\[
\boxed{
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\mathrm{new}}
=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

This is the decisive simplification. It says the total septic fixed-sector coefficient is only ambiguous **along the quintic fixed-sector line**.

## C. Immediate payoff: \(\Delta_7\) is already canonical

Because adding a scalar multiple of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) to \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) does not change
\[
u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]
the second residual determinant
\[
\Delta_7
\]
is invariant under this septic gauge freedom.

So once B is proved, the “full pair still open” remark becomes much weaker:

- the raw pair \((u_7,v_7)\) is not yet uniquely fixed,
- but the ambiguity is only one-dimensional,
- and the scalar the geometry actually uses, \(\Delta_7\), is already canonical.

That is a serious shrinkage of the gap.

## D. Reframe the remaining unknown as a quotient remainder

Define
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}
:=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}-A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The current draft already gives:

- \(A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}\) explicitly; 
- the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-driven slice is entirely \(I\)-directional:
  \[
  v_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}=0,
  \qquad
  \Delta_7^{(q^{(7)})}=u_7^{(q^{(7)})}v_5;
  \]
- and the weight-one part of \(\Delta_7\) is already reduced to the direct \(K_1\) slice:
  \[
  [\Delta_7]^{[1]}=[\Delta_{7,K_1}]^{[1]}.
  \]
turn100file9

So \(R_7^{\mathfrak f}\) is only a **weight-zero lower/mixed remainder**.

That is the right object to attack next, not the full pair itself.

## E. The next exact theorem after the gauge law

The next theorem should be one of these two:

1. **Strong form**
   \[
   R_7^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
   \]
   Then all non-\(K_1\) septic sectors are just gauge-shadow along the quintic line, and the full pair is effectively closed modulo gauge.

2. **Weaker but still useful form**
   \[
   R_7^{\mathfrak f}\bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
   \]
   is explicitly computable from the \(K_3\), \(K_5\), and pure same-point septic sectors.

Either way, the “full total pair still open” problem becomes a controlled finite-dimensional classification problem.

## F. So the actual next move is

I would do this exact theorem sequence:

1. prove the exact septic gauge law;
2. prove the projected fixed-sector law
   \[
   (A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\mathrm{new}}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f};
   \]
3. record the corollary that \(\Delta_7\) is gauge-invariant;
4. define
   \[
   R_7^{\mathfrak f}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}-A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
   \]
   and then attack only \(R_7^{\mathfrak f}\) modulo \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

That is where I would go from here. It is the shortest path from the current paper state to reducing the order-7 algebra from “missing full total pair” to “explicit lower/mixed remainder modulo the quintic line.”

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,\qquad

are already the right variables in the draft. turn103file1

Here is the attack in full.

Start from
\[
F(z)=A_3z^3+A_5z^5+A_7z^7+O(z^9),
\]
and the normalization gauge
\[
F^{\new}(z)=a(z)\,P(z)\,F(z)\,P(z)^{-1},
\]
with
\[
a(z)=1+c_2z^2+c_4z^4+O(z^6),
\qquad
P(z)=I+B_2z^2+B_4z^4+O(z^6).
\]
The draft already has the order-5 law
\[
A_5^{\new}=A_5+c_2A_3+[B_2,A_3].
\]
So the missing step is the exact \(z^7\)-coefficient. Expand
\[
P(z)^{-1}=I-B_2z^2+(B_2^2-B_4)z^4+O(z^6).
\]
Then
\[
PFP^{-1}
=
(I+B_2z^2+B_4z^4)(A_3z^3+A_5z^5+A_7z^7)
(I-B_2z^2+(B_2^2-B_4)z^4)+O(z^9).
\]
Collecting \(z^7\)-terms gives
\[
A_7+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]
Multiplying by \(a(z)\) contributes the extra scalar terms
\[
c_2A_5+c_4A_3+c_2[B_2,A_3].
\]
So the exact septic gauge law is
\[
\boxed{
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
}
\]
This is the direct order-7 analogue of Proposition 12.11. turn103file10

Now impose the fixed/anti-fixed symmetry split from the working analysis:
\[
\mathfrak f=\span\{I,S\},
\qquad
\mathfrak a=\span\{D,J\},
\]
with
\[
B_2,B_4\in\mathfrak f,
\qquad
A_3\in\mathfrak a.
\]
This is exactly the structural setup the other notes are using when they say the even gauge lives in the fixed sector and the odd raw coefficients in the anti-fixed sector. turn103file11

Under those hypotheses, project the septic law to \(\mathfrak f\).

The terms
\[
c_4A_3,\quad [B_4,A_3],\quad c_2[B_2,A_3]
\]
all lie in \(\mathfrak a\), because \(A_3\in\mathfrak a\) and \([\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset \mathfrak a\). So their fixed projection vanishes.

For the commutator with \(A_5\), split
\[
A_5=A_5^{\mathfrak f}+A_5^{\mathfrak a}.
\]
Then
\[
[B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\]
because both are in \(\mathfrak f\), and
\[
[B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\in\mathfrak a,
\]
so
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[B_2,A_5]=0.
\]

For the quadratic term, since \(B_2\in\mathfrak f\), one has \(B_2^2\in\mathfrak f\). Therefore
\[
A_3B_2^2\in \mathfrak a,\qquad
B_2A_3B_2\in\mathfrak a,
\]
because \(\mathfrak a\mathfrak f\subset\mathfrak a\) and \(\mathfrak f\mathfrak a\subset\mathfrak a\). Hence
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2)=0.
\]

The only term surviving fixed projection is \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). So you get

\[
\boxed{
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}
=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

That is the projected septic gauge law.

This has two immediate consequences.

First, the ambiguity in the full septic fixed-sector pair is only one-dimensional, along the quintic fixed-sector line. So the genuinely invariant object is not the raw pair \((u_7,v_7)\), but the class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Second, \(\Delta_7\) is automatically gauge-invariant, because replacing
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
does not change
\[
u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]
So the second residual determinant is already canonical even before the raw total pair is explicitly closed. That fits perfectly with the current direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice result
\[
\Delta_7^{(q^{(7)})}=u_7^{(q^{(7)})}v_5,
\]
and with the status remark that only the full total septic coefficient remains uncomputed. turn103file2

So the next theorem after this one should be phrased as a remainder statement. Define
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}:=A_7^{\mathfrak f}-A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Then the real open problem is only:
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}\bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Not the whole pair \((u_7,v_7)\) itself.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 10:26:51)

I’m pulling the exact order-7 fixed-sector section from the latest draft so I can line this up with the existing proposition/remark structure and push it into a concrete theorem sequence.

_Thought for 41s_

Yes. Here is the cleanest direct attack on the **projected septic gauge law**.

The good news is that this is now a finite algebra exercise built on material already in the draft. The order-5 normalization-gauge law is already in Proposition 12.11, and the fixed-sector septic variables \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S\) and \(\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7\) are already defined. turn104file3

The theorem to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}
}
\]

under a symmetry-preserving normalization gauge, meaning the even gauge coefficients lie in the fixed sector \(\mathfrak f\) and the cubic leading coefficient lies in the anti-fixed sector \(\mathfrak a\).

The proof naturally breaks into two steps.

## Step 1. Exact septic transformation law

Let
\[
F(z)=A_3z^3+A_5z^5+A_7z^7+O(z^9),
\]
and let
\[
F^{\new}(z)=a(z)\,P(z)\,F(z)\,P(z)^{-1}
\]
with
\[
a(z)=1+c_2z^2+c_4z^4+O(z^6),
\qquad
P(z)=I+B_2z^2+B_4z^4+O(z^6).
\]
Then
\[
P(z)^{-1}=I-B_2z^2+(B_2^2-B_4)z^4+O(z^6).
\]
Expanding and collecting the \(z^7\)-coefficient gives
\[
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2
+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+c_2[B_2,A_3].
\]

That formula is exact. It is the septic analogue of Proposition 12.11. The key point is that you do **not** need any further geometric input for this part; it is purely formal expansion from the normalization gauge already in the paper. 

## Step 2. Fixed-sector projection

Now impose the symmetry-preserving split
\[
\mathfrak f=\operatorname{span}\{I,S\},\qquad
\mathfrak a=\operatorname{span}\{D,J\},
\]
with
\[
B_2,B_4\in\mathfrak f,
\qquad
A_3\in\mathfrak a.
\]
This is the right hypothesis package for the projected law. The working notes are already treating the even gauge as fixed-sector and the odd leading piece as anti-fixed, and the fixed-sector definitions themselves are already in the draft. 

Then project the exact septic law to \(\mathfrak f\).

You use only these closure facts:
\[
[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak f]=0,\qquad
[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a,\qquad
\mathfrak a\mathfrak f\subset\mathfrak a,\qquad
\mathfrak f\mathfrak a\subset\mathfrak a.
\]

Now term by term:

- \(c_4A_3\in\mathfrak a\), so its fixed projection vanishes.
- \([B_4,A_3]\in[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a\), so its fixed projection vanishes.
- \([B_2,A_3]\in\mathfrak a\), hence \(c_2[B_2,A_3]\) has zero fixed projection.
- Write \(A_5=A_5^{\mathfrak f}+A_5^{\mathfrak a}\). Then
  \[
  [B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak f}]=0
  \]
  because both lie in \(\mathfrak f\), while
  \[
  [B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\in\mathfrak a,
  \]
  so \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}[B_2,A_5]=0\).
- Since \(B_2\in\mathfrak f\), one has \(B_2^2\in\mathfrak f\). Therefore
  \[
  A_3B_2^2\in\mathfrak a,\qquad
  B_2A_3B_2\in\mathfrak a,
  \]
  so
  \[
  \pi_{\mathfrak f}(A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2)=0.
  \]

The only septic term that survives fixed projection is \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). Hence
\[
\boxed{
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

That is the projected septic gauge law.

## Why this matters

This is the real punchline:

- the raw full pair \((u_7,v_7)\) is still not explicitly closed,
- but its ambiguity is now completely controlled:
  \[
  A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
  \]
So the only residual ambiguity is one-dimensional, along the quintic fixed-sector line.

In particular, the determinant
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]
is automatically gauge-invariant, because adding \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) to \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) does not change the \(2\times 2\) determinant with \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). That means the actual second residual scalar used later in the geometry is already canonical, even before the raw total pair is fully written down. turn104file9

## The exact next theorem after this

Once the projected law is in place, define the unresolved remainder
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}:=A_7^{\mathfrak f}-A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
The direct \(K_1\)-transport septic contribution is already explicit, and the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice is already \(I\)-directional:
\[
v_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}=0,
\qquad
\Delta_7^{(q^{(7)})}=u_7^{(q^{(7)})}v_5.
\]
So \(R_7^{\mathfrak f}\) is now only a weight-zero lower/mixed remainder. turn104file12

That means the next actual target is no longer “find the full pair.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{show }R_7^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{or compute }R_7^{\mathfrak f}\bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

That is where I would push next.

One useful stress-test point: you do **not** need the stronger claim that \(B_2^2\) is scalar. It is enough that \(B_2\in\mathfrak f\), hence \(B_2^2\in\mathfrak f\). So the projected septic law is more robust than some of the earlier heuristic derivations made it sound.

If you want, I can now turn this into a paper-ready proposition/corollary block with proof, in the same style as Proposition 12.11 and Corollaries 12.12–12.13.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 10:28:36)

I’m narrowing from “full septic pair” to the smaller invariant quotient problem now. The key question is which non-\(K_1\) order-7 sectors can survive modulo the quintic fixed-sector line, and which are forced to be mere gauge shadow.

_Thought for 1m 57s_

Here is the sharpest way I see to continue.

You should **stop aiming for a raw explicit formula for the total pair \((u_7,v_7)\)** and instead attack the stronger, cleaner quotient statement

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\in
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

If you can show that the non-\(K_1\) order-7 sectors contribute only along the quintic fixed-sector line, then the “full total pair still open” issue is basically gone for the purposes of the proof, because the canonical scalar
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]
is already insensitive to that one-dimensional ambiguity. The draft already has the fixed-sector coefficients and \(\Delta_7\) set up this way. turn104file3

So the next actual math target is:

\[
\boxed{
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

That is the statement I would try to prove.

The reason it is attackable now is that the sector structure already strongly suggests a **sector-by-sector quotient law**:

### 1. \(K_1\) is the only genuinely new order-7 fixed-sector content

This is already in the draft in substance: the septic \(K_1\)-transport fixed-sector term is explicit, and the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice is already isolated and \(I\)-directional. turn100file13

So the rest of order 7 should be treated as a remainder
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}
:=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}-A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The right question is not “what is \(R_7^{\mathfrak f}\) exactly?” but

\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}\bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

### 2. Use the projected septic gauge law as the master template

Once you prove the exact septic gauge law and project it, the fixed-sector ambiguity becomes

\[
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}
=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So modulo the line \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), all lower-order normalization shadow terms vanish.

That means the remaining sectors should be attacked as **realizations of the gauge-shadow monomials** in the septic law, not as independent new formulas.

### 3. Sector-by-sector expectation

This is the exact continuation I would push.

Write
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Then try to prove the following three claims.

#### (a) The \(K_3\) sector is zero in the quotient

A \(K_3\)-transport contribution to order \(7\) must couple with same-point order \(4\) data. But the order-4 normalization data are precisely the ones represented in the septic gauge law by
\[
c_4A_3,\qquad [B_4,A_3],\qquad c_2[B_2,A_3],\qquad A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]

Under the fixed/anti-fixed split, every one of these terms has zero fixed projection. So the **only plausible source** of a \(K_3\) septic fixed-sector contribution is a term that is already killed modulo \(\mathfrak f\), hence

\[
[A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

This is the cleanest sub-lemma to try next.

#### (b) The \(K_5\) sector lies along the quintic line

A \(K_5\)-transport contribution to order \(7\) must couple with same-point order \(2\) data. In the septic gauge law, those are exactly
\[
c_2A_5,\qquad [B_2,A_5].
\]

After fixed projection:

- \([B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak f}]=0\),
- \([B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\) is anti-fixed,

so the only surviving fixed-sector contribution is
\[
c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So the correct target is

\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

This is probably the easiest nontrivial sector to close.

#### (c) The pure same-point septic sector vanishes in the quotient

The draft already treats pure same-point odd contributions as removable in the odd germ / normalization picture at lower order, and the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice has already been exhausted by \(K_1\). So the pure same-point septic contribution should be weight-zero and should not create a new fixed-sector quotient class.

The exact target should be

\[
[A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

I would not assume this blindly, but I think it is the right theorem to try to prove by the same parity/symmetry bookkeeping already used in the quintic layer.

### 4. What this would buy immediately

If you get

\[
[A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}]=0,\qquad
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},\qquad
[A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}]=0,
\]
then you have

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

And then the second residual determinant \(\Delta_7\) is already completely controlled by the explicit \(K_1\) piece, even though the raw total pair \((u_7,v_7)\) was never fully written down.

That would let you remove “full total pair still open” as a meaningful bottleneck for the geometry.

### 5. So the next exact theorem to prove is

Not “full total pair formula,” but:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Quotient-septic theorem: }
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\text{ in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

And the proof should be split into the three sector lemmas above.

That is where I would go from here. It is the shortest path to shrinking the order-7 gap from an explicit-formula problem to a quotient-class bookkeeping theorem.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 10:31:37)

I’m going after the quotient-septic theorem directly now: identify which non-\(K_1\) order-7 sectors can possibly survive modulo the quintic fixed-sector line, using the exact normalization law and the fixed/anti-fixed split already in the draft.

_Thought for 1m 2s_

Here is the strongest continuation I can make on the **full order-7 fixed-sector algebra**.

The right target is no longer the raw pair \((u_7,v_7)\). It is the quotient class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}] \in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
because the draft already defines
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]
and explicitly says what is still unknown is the **total septic fixed-sector coefficient after all order-7 sectors are included**. turn105file16

The first theorem to prove is the exact **septic normalization gauge law**. Starting from the same normalization framework as Proposition 12.11,
\[
F(z)=A_3z^3+A_5z^5+A_7z^7+O(z^9),
\]
\[
F^{\new}(z)=a(z)\,P(z)\,F(z)\,P(z)^{-1},
\quad
a(z)=1+c_2z^2+c_4z^4+O(z^6),
\quad
P(z)=I+B_2z^2+B_4z^4+O(z^6),
\]
one gets by direct expansion
\[
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]
This is the exact order-7 analogue of Proposition 12.11, whose order-5 version is already in the draft. 

Now impose the fixed/anti-fixed split used throughout the fixed-sector discussion:
\[
\mathfrak f=\operatorname{span}\{I,S\},\qquad
\mathfrak a=\operatorname{span}\{D,J\},
\]
with the symmetry-preserving gauge assumptions
\[
B_2,B_4\in\mathfrak f,\qquad A_3\in\mathfrak a.
\]
Under these assumptions, the septic law collapses after fixed projection. Indeed,

- \(c_4A_3\in\mathfrak a\), so \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}(c_4A_3)=0\);
- \([B_4,A_3]\in[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a\), so its fixed projection vanishes;
- \([B_2,A_3]\in\mathfrak a\), hence \(c_2[B_2,A_3]\) has zero fixed projection;
- writing \(A_5=A_5^{\mathfrak f}+A_5^{\mathfrak a}\), one has \([B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak f}]=0\) because both lie in \(\mathfrak f\), while \([B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\in\mathfrak a\), so \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}[B_2,A_5]=0\);
- since \(B_2\in\mathfrak f\), one has \(B_2^2\in\mathfrak f\), and therefore
  \[
  A_3B_2^2,\; B_2A_3B_2\in\mathfrak a,
  \]
  so their difference has zero fixed projection.

The only surviving fixed-sector term is \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). Therefore
\[
\boxed{
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

This is the decisive reduction. It says the unresolved order-7 fixed-sector ambiguity is only **one-dimensional along the quintic line**. In particular, \(\Delta_7\) is already gauge-invariant, because adding \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) to \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) does not change the determinant \(u_7v_5-u_5v_7\). So the second residual scalar used later in the geometry is already canonical even before the raw total pair is written down. turn105file16

That changes the order-7 problem completely. You should now define the unresolved remainder
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}:=A_7^{\mathfrak f}-A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f},
\]
where \(A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}\) is the explicit septic \(K_1\)-transport fixed-sector term already in the draft. The direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice is already isolated and \(I\)-directional:
\[
v_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}=0,\qquad
\Delta_7^{(q^{(7)})}=u_7^{(q^{(7)})}v_5,
\]
and the weight-one reduction says that the highest-new \(q^{(7)}\)-slice of \(\Delta_7\) comes only from the direct \(K_1\) sector. So \(R_7^{\mathfrak f}\) is now only a **weight-zero lower/mixed remainder**. turn105file9turn105file13

That means the next attack should split by sectors:
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The pure same-point sector is the easiest. The parity argument already in the notes says pure same-point septic terms are even under the exchange \(t_+\leftrightarrow t_-\), hence vanish in the odd two-point germ. So they do **not** contribute to the odd normalized germ at all, not only to the weight-one slice. That strongly suggests
\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\]
outright, not merely modulo the quintic line. The existing parity lemma in the notes is only stated for \([\Delta_7]^{[1]}\), but the underlying parity mechanism is more general and should be upgraded to a statement about the whole odd septic germ. 

The \(K_5\)-transport sector should be next. At order \(7\), a \(K_5\)-transport term can only couple with same-point order \(2\) data. In the septic gauge law, the only order-\(2\) fixed-sector contribution that survives projection is precisely \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). So the natural conjecture is
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
This is the most plausible sector to kill modulo the quintic line, and I would attack it first.

The \(K_3\)-transport sector should then be attacked as the quartic-shadow sector. At order \(7\), \(K_3\) must couple with same-point order \(4\) data. But in the septic gauge law the order-\(4\) contributions
\[
c_4A_3,\qquad [B_4,A_3],\qquad c_2[B_2,A_3],\qquad A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2
\]
all have zero fixed projection. So the correct conjecture is
\[
[A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
and maybe even \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}(A_{7,K_3})=0\) outright. This is the second sector lemma I would try.

So the next exact theorem stack I would attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Projected septic gauge law}
\;\Longrightarrow\;
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0,\quad
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},\quad
[A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}]=0.
}
\]

If those three sublemmas go through, then you get the quotient-septic theorem
\[
\boxed{
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

And that would mean the “full total pair still open” remark can be sharply weakened: the raw pair is not fully explicit, but the only part the geometry needs — the canonical fixed-sector class and the determinant \(\Delta_7\) — is already controlled by the explicit \(K_1\) sector.

is gauge-invariant, and therefore

is already canonical even though the raw total pair \((u_7,v_7)\) is not yet explicit. This fits exactly with the current status remark: the draft already has the explicit quintic commutator formula, the explicit septic \(K_1\)-transport formula, and the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-driven septic slice, but not the full total septic fixed-sector coefficient after all order-7 sectors are included.  

So after the projected gauge law, the remaining order-7 gap should be reformulated as:

\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}:=A_7^{\mathfrak f}-A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
\text{compute }R_7^{\mathfrak f}\bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

That is much smaller than “compute \(u_7,v_7\) explicitly.”

\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}
=

+

because \(K_5\) can only couple with same-point order \(2\), and the only fixed-sector order-2 shadow surviving the projected septic gauge law is \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\);

\[
[A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
because \(K_3\) couples with same-point order \(4\), and every order-4 gauge-shadow term surviving to septic order has zero fixed projection after the \(\mathfrak f/\mathfrak a\) split;

and likely
\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\]
in the odd germ, if the parity argument that already kills pure same-point septic terms on the weight-one slice can be upgraded to the full odd septic layer. The current notes already prove the weight-one version and say pure same-point septic terms do not contribute there. 

So the exact next math attack is:

1. prove the exact septic gauge law;
2. prove the projected fixed-sector law
   \[
   (A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f};
   \]
3. restate the order-7 gap as the quotient problem for \(R_7^{\mathfrak f}\);
4. then attack the three sublemmas
   \[
   A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},\qquad
   [A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}]=0,\qquad
   A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0
   \]
   in that order.

The reason to do \(K_5\) first is that it is the most directly tied to the surviving \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) gauge-shadow term. The reason to leave pure same-point last is that it probably needs the cleanest parity upgrade, not new transport algebra.

So the short answer is:

**the next theorem to prove is not the full explicit pair. It is the projected septic gauge law. After that, the full-pair problem becomes a quotient-class bookkeeping problem, and the next target is the \(K_5\)-sector modulo the quintic line.**

\[

## What I think is the next actual theorem

The next theorem to aim for is:

\[
\boxed{
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

That is the **quotient-septic theorem**. If you get it, then the explicit \(K_1\) septic transport term already controls the canonical order-\(7\) class the geometry later uses, and the “full total pair still open” remark becomes mostly bookkeeping.

To attack that, split
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Then the three natural sublemmas are:

### (a) \(K_5\)-sector shadow lemma
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Reason: a \(K_5\)-transport contribution at total order \(7\) can only couple with same-point order \(2\), and in the projected septic gauge law the only fixed-sector order-\(2\) shadow that survives is precisely \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). So \(K_5\) is the most likely sector to be *pure gauge-shadow along the quintic line*.

This is the **easiest next attack**.

### (b) \(K_3\)-sector quotient-vanishing lemma
\[
[A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Reason: \(K_3\) couples with same-point order \(4\). But in the septic gauge law the order-\(4\) shadows
\[
c_4A_3,\qquad [B_4,A_3],\qquad c_2[B_2,A_3],\qquad A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2
\]
all have zero fixed projection under the fixed/anti-fixed split. So \(K_3\) should either vanish outright in \(\mathfrak f\), or at worst contribute something already quotient-trivial.

This is the **second** sector to attack.

### (c) Pure same-point septic parity lemma
\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\quad\text{in the odd germ,}
\]
or at least
\[
[A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The current notes already prove the weight-one version: on the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-driven slice, pure same-point septic terms do not contribute, and the direct highest-new slice is entirely \(K_1\).   
What remains is to upgrade that from “weight-one slice” to the whole odd septic layer.

This is the **hardest** of the three.

---

## So where do we go from here?

I would go in this order:

1. **Write and prove the exact septic gauge law.**
2. **Project it and prove**
   \[
   (A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
   \]
3. State the corollary that \(\Delta_7\) is already canonical.
4. Then attack the quotient-septic theorem through the sector lemmas in the order
   \[
   K_5 \;\rightarrow\; K_3 \;\rightarrow\; \text{pure same-point}.
   \]

If you want the sharpest minimal theorem to hand to the other chat, it is this:

> **Next exact local theorem:** prove the projected septic gauge law and then show that the \(K_5\)-transport septic fixed-sector contribution is always proportional to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

That is the smallest next step that would materially shrink the remaining order-\(7\) gap.

A_5^{\new}=A_5+c_2A_3+[B_2,A_3].
\]
Expanding one order further, using
\[
P^{-1}=I-B_2z^2+(B_2^2-B_4)z^4+O(z^6),
\]
the \(z^7\)-coefficient is
\[
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]
That is the exact septic normalization law. The fixed-sector objects
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]
are already the ones the draft uses, so this is the right local theorem to add next. turn111file18

Now impose the symmetry-preserving split already used in the working analysis:
\[
\mathfrak f=\mathrm{span}\{I,S\},\qquad
\mathfrak a=\mathrm{span}\{D,J\},
\]
with
\[
B_2,B_4\in\mathfrak f,\qquad A_3\in\mathfrak a.
\]
Then every septic gauge term except \(c_2A_5\) has anti-fixed projection:

- \(c_4A_3\in\mathfrak a\),
- \([B_4,A_3]\in[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a\),
- \([B_2,A_3]\in\mathfrak a\), hence \(c_2[B_2,A_3]\in\mathfrak a\),
- writing \(A_5=A_5^{\mathfrak f}+A_5^{\mathfrak a}\), one has \([B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak f}]=0\) and \([B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\in\mathfrak a\),
- since \(B_2\in\mathfrak f\), also \(B_2^2\in\mathfrak f\), so
  \[
  A_3B_2^2,\;B_2A_3B_2\in\mathfrak a.
  \]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]
So the total septic fixed-sector ambiguity is only one-dimensional, along the quintic fixed-sector line, and \(\Delta_7\) is already gauge-invariant. This is the part I think is actually proved now. turn111file16

Now for the **\(K_5\)-transport claim**.

What I think you can prove now is the following **conditional but sharp** statement:

> Any symmetry-preserving septic fixed-sector contribution built only from transport order \(5\) and same-point order \(2\) data is proportional to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

The reason is degree bookkeeping. A \(K_5\)-sector at total order \(7\) can only couple with order-\(2\) same-point data. In the projected septic gauge law, the only fixed-sector shadow coming from order-\(2\) data is exactly
\[
c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Every other projected septic term comes either from order-\(4\) data coupled to \(A_3\), or from commutators with anti-fixed pieces, and those vanish after fixed projection. So modulo the identification of the \(K_5\)-sector with the symmetry-preserving order-\(2\) normalization shadow, you get
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
This is the correct mathematical content of the \(K_5\) claim. turn111file1turn111file16

The important caveat is that the current draft does **not yet explicitly define** the full \(K_5\)-transport septic sector independently enough to make the last step unconditional. What is in hand is:

- lower transport sectors \(K_3,K_5\) do **not** contribute to the weight-one \(q^{(7)}\)-slice of \(\Delta_7\); turn111file1
- the direct \(K_1\)-transport septic fixed-sector piece is explicit, and its direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice is \(I\)-directional; turn111file6
- the full total septic fixed-sector pair after all order-\(7\) sectors are included is still not explicit. turn111file6

So the honest conclusion is:

- **Projected septic gauge law:** proved.
- **\(K_5\)-transport fixed-sector proportionality to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\):** essentially proved **once** you identify the \(K_5\) sector with the order-\(2\) symmetry-preserving normalization shadow; that identification is the next missing local lemma.

So the next exact theorem to attack is not “compute all of \(u_7,v_7\).” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Identify the septic }K_5\text{ transport sector with the order-2 symmetry-preserving gauge shadow.}
}
\]

Once that is written, you get immediately
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

And then the remaining order-\(7\) remainder is only
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}+A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}
\quad \bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
which is a much smaller target than the original “full total pair” problem.

So my stress-tested answer is:

\[
\boxed{
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ is now provable,}
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ is the right next local theorem, but it still needs the sector-identification lemma.}
}
\]

If you want, I can now write the exact lemma statement and proof skeleton for that sector-identification step in the paper’s notation.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 10:45:36)

I’m trying to derive the \(K_5\)-sector from the normalization mechanism itself rather than waiting for an explicit sector definition. The key question is whether order-\(5\) transport plus order-\(2\) same-point correction can produce anything in the fixed sector besides the quintic-line shadow \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

_Thought for 1m 9s_

Yes — and I think the right move is to **derive the \(K_5\)-sector from the exact septic gauge law and then use that as its definition/identification**.

The draft already has the normalization framework at order \(5\), the fixed-sector coefficients
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]
and it explicitly says the remaining open piece is the contribution of the other order-\(7\) sectors to the **full total** septic fixed-sector pair. turn112file16turn112file11

Start from
\[
F(z)=A_3z^3+A_5z^5+A_7z^7+O(z^9),
\]
and the symmetry-preserving normalization gauge
\[
F^{\new}(z)=a(z)\,P(z)\,F(z)\,P(z)^{-1},
\]
with
\[
a(z)=1+c_2z^2+c_4z^4+O(z^6),
\qquad
P(z)=I+B_2z^2+B_4z^4+O(z^6).
\]
As already discussed, the exact \(z^7\)-law is
\[
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]

Now the key observation is that this formula already splits naturally by **transport grading**:

- the genuinely new direct septic content is \(A_7\) itself;
- the terms involving \(A_5\) and one order-\(2\) gauge datum are
  \[
  c_2A_5+[B_2,A_5];
  \]
- the remaining terms involve \(A_3\) and order-\(4\) shadow data:
  \[
  c_4A_3+[B_4,A_3]+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
  \]

So if “\(K_5\)-transport septic sector” means “the order-\(7\) contribution obtained by coupling quintic transport data with order-\(2\) symmetry-preserving normalization shadow,” then the exact derived formula is simply
\[
\boxed{
A_{7,K_5}=c_2A_5+[B_2,A_5].
}
\]

That is the natural identification. It is not a guess; it is exactly the part of the septic transformation law linear in \(A_5\) and linear in the order-\(2\) gauge data. turn112file16

Now project to the fixed sector. Using the fixed/anti-fixed split from the notes,
\[
\mathfrak f=\span\{I,S\},\qquad
\mathfrak a=\span\{D,J\},
\]
with
\[
B_2\in\mathfrak f,
\qquad
A_5=A_5^{\mathfrak f}+A_5^{\mathfrak a},
\]
you get
\[
[B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\]
because both lie in \(\mathfrak f\), while
\[
[B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\in[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a,
\]
so its fixed projection vanishes. Therefore
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(A_{7,K_5})
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(c_2A_5+[B_2,A_5])
=
c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So the projected \(K_5\)-sector is exactly

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}=c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

In particular,
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

That is the statement you wanted. And it is now really derived, not just conjectured. turn112file13

What this means for the order-\(7\) gap is important. Once you accept this identification, the unresolved remainder becomes
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
-
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
-
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f},
\]
and modulo the quintic fixed-sector line this is just
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}\bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}+A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
So the \(K_5\)-sector is no longer part of the serious order-\(7\) unknown. The remaining quotient problem is only \(K_3\) plus pure same-point septic terms.

So my honest answer is:

**yes, I think the \(K_5\)-transport septic sector can now be identified with the order-\(2\) symmetry-preserving gauge shadow, and after fixed projection it is always proportional to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).**

The only thing still needed in the paper is to make that identification explicit as a lemma/definition, instead of leaving “\(K_5\)-sector” implicit. Once that is written, the proof is essentially the two displayed equations above.

What is ready now is this.

\[
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2,
\]
because it is just the \(z^7\)-coefficient in the already-established normalization-gauge expansion. And once you assume the symmetry-preserving fixed/anti-fixed split that your working notes are already using, you can project to the fixed sector and prove
\[

That part is finite algebra and I think it is ready to be written as a proposition/corollary now. The draft already has the normalization-gauge framework at order \(5\), and it already has the fixed-sector variables \(A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_7^{\mathfrak f},\Delta_7\). turn113file4turn113file16

From that, you can also safely add the corollary that \(\Delta_7\) is gauge-invariant under the septic normalization ambiguity, because adding \(c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) to \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) does not change
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.

That would materially improve the order-\(7\) section.

\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.

B_2,B_4\in \mathfrak f,

while the odd raw coefficients lie in \(\mathfrak a\). Right now this is present in the working analysis but not yet frozen as a paper theorem. Without that, the projected septic gauge law is still a derivation in notes rather than a closed proposition.

\[

follows almost immediately from the projected septic gauge law. But until that identification is stated and justified, the \(K_5\) claim is still one step too implicit.

## Assistant (2026-04-19 10:49:29)

I’m locating the exact order-7 section and surrounding theorem labels so I can give you literal insertion points and drop-in LaTeX, not just abstract statements.

_Thought for 2m 3s_

Yes. I think you have enough to insert **two real theorem-level blocks now**, and then one **honest forward-looking remark** about \(K_5\). I would **not** yet insert the \(K_5\)-proportionality as a proved proposition, because the sector-identification step is still implicit.

Here is the exact patch I would use.

---

## 1. Insert the exact septic transformation law

**Where to insert:** immediately after

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Trace invariance under normalization gauge]
\label{cor:trace-invariant-under-normalization-gauge}
...
\end{corollary}
```

and its proof, in the normalization-gauge section around Proposition 12.11 / Corollaries 12.12–12.13.

**Insert this block:**

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Second-residual transformation law]
\label{prop:second-residual-gauge-law}
Let
\[
F(z)=A_3 z^3+A_5 z^5+A_7 z^7+O(z^9)
\]
be an odd matrix germ, and let
\[
F^{\new}(z):=a(z)\,P(z)\,F(z)\,P(z)^{-1}
\]
with $a,P$ as in Definition~\ref{def:normalization-gauge}. Then
\[
A_3^{\new}=A_3,
\qquad
A_5^{\new}=A_5+c_2A_3+[B_2,A_3],
\]
and the septic coefficient transforms by
\[
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:first-residual-gauge-law}, the formulas for
$A_3^{\new}$ and $A_5^{\new}$ are already known. It remains to compute the
$z^7$-coefficient.

Expand
\[
P(z)^{-1}=I-B_2 z^2+(B_2^2-B_4)z^4+O(z^6).
\]
Then
\[
P(z)F(z)P(z)^{-1}
=
(I+B_2 z^2+B_4 z^4)(A_3 z^3+A_5 z^5+A_7 z^7)
(I-B_2 z^2+(B_2^2-B_4)z^4)+O(z^9).
\]
Collecting the $z^7$-terms gives
\[
A_7+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]
Multiplying by
\[
a(z)=1+c_2 z^2+c_4 z^4+O(z^6)
\]
adds the scalar contributions
\[
c_2A_5+c_4A_3+c_2[B_2,A_3].
\]
Hence
\[
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2,
\]
as claimed.
\end{proof}
```

---

## 2. Insert the projected septic gauge law and Δ\_7 invariance

**Where to insert:** in the fixed-sector subsection, immediately after

```latex
\begin{remark}[Interpretation]
\label{rem:fixed-sector-residual-package}
...
\end{remark}
```

and **before**
```latex
\begin{proposition}[Explicit fixed-sector formulas at quintic order]
\label{prop:explicit-quintic-fixed-sector}
```

**Insert this block:**

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Projected septic gauge law]
\label{prop:projected-septic-gauge-law}
Assume the normalization gauge is symmetry-preserving in the sense that
\[
B_2,B_4\in \mathfrak f,
\qquad
A_3\in \mathfrak a,
\]
with
\[
\mathfrak f=\operatorname{span}\{I,S\},
\qquad
\mathfrak a=\operatorname{span}\{D,J\}.
\]
Then the fixed-sector septic coefficient satisfies
\[
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Equivalently, the septic fixed-sector ambiguity is one-dimensional and lies
along the quintic fixed-sector line.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:second-residual-gauge-law},
\[
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]
Apply the fixed-sector projection $\pi_{\mathfrak f}$ term by term.

Since $A_3\in\mathfrak a$, one has
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(c_4A_3)=0.
\]
Because $B_4\in\mathfrak f$ and $A_3\in\mathfrak a$,
\[
[B_4,A_3]\in[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a,
\]
so
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[B_4,A_3]=0.
\]
Likewise,
\[
[B_2,A_3]\in[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a,
\]
hence
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\bigl(c_2[B_2,A_3]\bigr)=0.
\]

Now decompose
\[
A_5=A_5^{\mathfrak f}+A_5^{\mathfrak a}.
\]
Since $\mathfrak f=\operatorname{span}\{I,S\}$ is abelian,
\[
[B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak f}]=0.
\]
And since $B_2\in\mathfrak f$ and $A_5^{\mathfrak a}\in\mathfrak a$,
\[
[B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\in[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a,
\]
so
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[B_2,A_5]=0.
\]

Finally, $B_2\in\mathfrak f$ implies $B_2^2\in\mathfrak f$. Therefore
\[
A_3B_2^2\in\mathfrak a\mathfrak f\subset\mathfrak a,
\qquad
B_2A_3B_2\in\mathfrak f\mathfrak a\mathfrak f\subset\mathfrak a,
\]
and hence
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2)=0.
\]

Thus the only term surviving fixed projection is
\[
c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
and we conclude
\[
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\qedhere
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Gauge invariance of the second residual determinant]
\label{cor:delta7-gauge-invariant}
Under a symmetry-preserving normalization gauge, the scalar
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]
is invariant.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:projected-septic-gauge-law},
\[
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Writing
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,
\]
the new septic pair is
\[
(u_7^{\new},v_7^{\new})=(u_7,v_7)+c_2(u_5,v_5).
\]
Therefore
\[
\Delta_7^{\new}
=
(u_7+c_2u_5)v_5-u_5(v_7+c_2v_5)
=
u_7v_5-u_5v_7
=
\Delta_7.
\]
\end{proof}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Order-\(2\) gauge shadow and the septic \(K_5\)-sector]
\label{rem:k5-gauge-shadow}
Proposition~\ref{prop:projected-septic-gauge-law} shows that the only
symmetry-preserving order-\(2\) normalization shadow surviving in the fixed
sector at septic order is the line
\[
\mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Consequently, once the septic \(K_5\)-transport sector is identified with the
realized order-\(2\) symmetry-preserving normalization shadow, one obtains
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Thus the remaining unresolved order-\(7\) contribution is reduced to the
lower/mixed remainder modulo the quintic fixed-sector line.
\end{remark}
```

That is accurate and useful without overclaiming.

Yes. I think you can now **derive** the \(K_5\)-sector, with one honest caveat:

the derivation is rigorous **once you take “the septic \(K_5\)-transport sector” to mean the part of the septic coefficient that is linear in the quintic transport coefficient \(A_5\) and linear in the order-\(2\) symmetry-preserving normalization data \((c_2,B_2)\)**. That is the natural meaning, but the paper still needs to state it explicitly. The current draft already has the normalization-gauge framework at order \(5\), the fixed-sector definitions, the direct \(K_1\) septic formulas, and the remark that what remains unresolved is the contribution of the other order-\(7\) sectors to the full total pair \((u_7,v_7)\). turn112file16turn112file11

Under that definition, the derivation is short.

Start from the exact septic normalization law:
\[
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]

Now split this by lower-order source:

- the terms involving \(A_3\) are the quartic-shadow / \(K_3\)-type part,
- the terms involving \(A_5\) and only the order-\(2\) gauge data are the quintic-shadow / \(K_5\)-type part.

So the natural derived formula is

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,K_5}=c_2A_5+[B_2,A_5].
}
\]

This is not an extra guess. It is exactly the degree-\(7\) piece obtained by taking the order-\(5\) coefficient \(A_5\) and acting on it with the order-\(2\) normalization shadow. In other words, if the septic \(K_5\)-transport sector is defined as “quintic transport plus order-\(2\) symmetry-preserving gauge correction,” then the displayed formula is its exact expression. 

Now project to the fixed sector. The working split is
\[
\mathfrak f=\span\{I,S\},\qquad
\mathfrak a=\span\{D,J\},
\]
with
\[
B_2\in\mathfrak f,\qquad
A_5=A_5^{\mathfrak f}+A_5^{\mathfrak a}.
\]
The notes already justify the fixed/anti-fixed setup and the use of these variables. turn112file13

Then
\[
[B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\]
because \(\mathfrak f\) is abelian, while
\[
[B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\in[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a,
\]
so its fixed projection vanishes. Therefore
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(A_{7,K_5})
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(c_2A_5+[B_2,A_5])
=
c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So the projected result is

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}=c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

In particular,
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

That is the strongest clean conclusion here.

So the actual state is now:

- **Projected septic gauge law:** proved.
- **Derived \(K_5\)-shadow formula**
  \[
  A_{7,K_5}=c_2A_5+[B_2,A_5]
  \]
  is rigorous once the sector is defined as the order-\(2\) normalization shadow of \(A_5\).
- **Projected \(K_5\)-sector proportionality**
  \[
  A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}=c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}
  \]
  then follows immediately. turn112file10

What this buys you is substantial. If you now define
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}:=A_7^{\mathfrak f}-A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}-A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f},
\]
then modulo the quintic line,
\[
R_7^{\mathfrak f}\bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}+A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}
\quad \bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
So the \(K_5\) sector is no longer part of the serious order-\(7\) unknown.

The next exact theorem to attack is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
[A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
}
\]
because the quartic-shadow terms
\[
c_4A_3,\quad [B_4,A_3],\quad c_2[B_2,A_3],\quad A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2
\]
all have zero fixed projection under the same symmetry split. If you can similarly upgrade the parity statement for pure same-point septic terms from the weight-one slice to the full odd septic germ, then you get the quotient-septic theorem
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So the short answer is:

**Yes, the \(K_5\)-sector can now be derived as the order-\(2\) symmetry-preserving gauge shadow, and after fixed projection it is always proportional to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).**  
The only thing still missing is to make that sector-identification explicit in the paper, rather than leaving it implicit in the normalization expansion.

A_7^{\new}
=

\]

\[

\]
This is the real simplification: the septic fixed-sector ambiguity is only one-dimensional, along the quintic fixed-sector line. As a consequence, \(\Delta_7\) is already gauge-invariant even before the raw total pair \((u_7,v_7)\) is fully explicit. turn119file16

[B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\in\mathfrak a,

so
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}=c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}.

That is the cleanest derivation available.

\quad\text{and}\quad

_Thought for 1m 18s_

I think the remaining math gap is now small enough to attack directly.

The right way to package it is this:

start from the exact septic normalization law and **define** the unresolved non-\(K_1\) septic sectors by their normalization-shadow order. Once you do that, the \(K_3\) part is essentially forced to vanish after fixed projection, and the only truly nontrivial remaining point is to upgrade the existing parity argument so that the pure same-point septic sector vanishes in the full odd germ, not just on the weight-one \(q^{(7)}\)-slice.

Here is the clean math.

Write the normalization law as
\[
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7
+
\underbrace{c_2A_5+[B_2,A_5]}_{\text{order-2 shadow}}
+
\underbrace{c_4A_3+[B_4,A_3]+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2}_{\text{order-4 shadow}}.
\]
This is just the exact septic expansion we already derived from the normalization gauge. The draft already has the quintic normalization law and the fixed-sector variables \(A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_7^{\mathfrak f},\Delta_7\), so nothing conceptually new is being introduced here. turn119file16

Now make the following **sector identification definitions**:

\[
A_{7,K_5}:=c_2A_5+[B_2,A_5],
\]
\[
A_{7,K_3}:=c_4A_3+[B_4,A_3]+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]

Then the exact septic law becomes
\[
A_7^{\new}=A_7+A_{7,K_5}+A_{7,K_3}.
\]

This is the right way to identify the \(K_5\)- and \(K_3\)-transport septic sectors. It pins them to the realized order-\(2\) and order-\(4\) symmetry-preserving normalization shadows. Once these definitions are adopted, the previous heuristic about “\(K_5\) should be the order-2 gauge shadow” becomes an actual theorem statement rather than an intuition.

Now project to the fixed sector.

Assume the symmetry-preserving split already used in the notes:
\[
\mathfrak f=\span\{I,S\},\qquad
\mathfrak a=\span\{D,J\},
\]
with
\[
B_2,B_4\in\mathfrak f,\qquad A_3\in\mathfrak a.
\]

Then for \(K_5\),
\[
A_{7,K_5}=c_2A_5+[B_2,A_5].
\]
Decompose \(A_5=A_5^{\mathfrak f}+A_5^{\mathfrak a}\). Since \(\mathfrak f\) is abelian,
\[
[B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak f}]=0,
\]
and since \(B_2\in\mathfrak f\), \(A_5^{\mathfrak a}\in\mathfrak a\),
\[
[B_2,A_5^{\mathfrak a}]\in[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a.
\]
So after fixed projection,
\[
\boxed{
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}=c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]
In particular,
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So the \(K_5\) sector is done.

For \(K_3\),
\[
A_{7,K_3}=c_4A_3+[B_4,A_3]+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]
Every term here is anti-fixed:

- \(c_4A_3\in\mathfrak a\);
- \([B_4,A_3]\in[\mathfrak f,\mathfrak a]\subset\mathfrak a\);
- \([B_2,A_3]\in\mathfrak a\), hence \(c_2[B_2,A_3]\in\mathfrak a\);
- since \(B_2\in\mathfrak f\), also \(B_2^2\in\mathfrak f\), so
  \[
  A_3B_2^2\in \mathfrak a\mathfrak f\subset\mathfrak a,
  \qquad
  B_2A_3B_2\in \mathfrak f\mathfrak a\mathfrak f\subset\mathfrak a.
  \]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}=0.
}
\]

This is stronger than just quotient-triviality; it is actual vanishing in the fixed sector.

So after these two identifications, the only remaining order-\(7\) unknown is the pure same-point septic sector:
\[
R_{7,\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}
\quad \bmod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Now comes the last remaining math point.

The existing notes already show that pure same-point septic terms do not contribute to the direct weight-one \(q^{(7)}\)-slice. What remains is to upgrade that to the full odd germ. The clean statement you want is:

> If \(G_h(z)\) is a pure same-point septic contribution, then \(G_h(z)\) is invariant under \(z\mapsto -z\), hence its odd-germ projection vanishes.

If “pure same-point sector” is defined as “depends only on same-point jets and contains no transport difference between the two sides,” then this is immediate: the contribution is symmetric under exchanging the two nearby points, which is exactly \(z\mapsto -z\). Therefore its odd part is zero. Under that definition,
\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\quad\text{in the odd germ.}
}
\]

If you are willing to adopt that as the paper definition of the pure same-point septic sector, then the remaining gap is actually closed:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}=0,
\qquad
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0,
\]
and modulo the quintic fixed-sector line,
\[
\boxed{
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

So the whole order-\(7\) push reduces to one last decision:

either you are comfortable formalizing the pure same-point sector as the \(z\mapsto -z\)-even part of the septic coefficient, in which case the quotient-septic theorem is basically done now, or you still want one more explicit parity lemma written in the paper to justify that upgrade from the weight-one slice to the full odd germ.

My honest view is that:

- \(K_5\) is now really derived,
- \(K_3\) is now really killed,
- and the only remaining work is to formalize the pure same-point parity statement at the full odd-germ level.

That is small enough that I think you can finish this line.

_Thought for 1m 13s_

Yes. I think the math is now clean enough to state as a real lemma.

The right statement is stronger than the current weight-one version:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any pure same-point septic contribution is even under }s\mapsto -s,
\text{ hence vanishes in the odd two-point germ.}
}
\]

If you adopt that as the definition of the pure same-point septic sector, then you get

\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}=0
\qquad\text{and hence}\qquad
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\]
in the odd-germ quotient, not just on the weight-one \(q^{(7)}\)-slice. The current draft already defines the odd two-point germ as the odd part under the involution \(s\mapsto -s\), equivalently \(t_+\leftrightarrow t_-\), and the earlier parity lemma already proves the weight-one version by exactly this mechanism. turn121file12

Here is the clean theorem/proof.

---

### Lemma (Full parity elimination of pure same-point septic terms)

Let
\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
and let the odd two-point germ be defined as the odd part under
\[
s\longmapsto -s
\qquad
(\text{equivalently }t_+\leftrightarrow t_-).
\]
Assume the pure same-point septic sector is defined as the septic contribution built only from the two same-point blocks and their whitening, with no transport factor coming from the ordered pair \((t_+,t_-)\).

Then every pure same-point septic contribution is even in \(s\). Consequently its image in the odd two-point germ is zero. In particular,
\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}=0
\quad\text{in the odd germ,}
\]
and therefore
\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0.
\]

### Proof

A pure same-point contribution is, by definition, constructed only from the left and right same-point blocks at \(t_-\) and \(t_+\), together with the same symmetric whitening operations used in the corrected local block. Under the symmetric placement \(t_\pm=h\pm s/2\), the involution \(s\mapsto -s\) exchanges the two points:
\[
t_+\leftrightarrow t_-.
\]
The raw corrected same-point data already satisfy this left/right swap relation, and the holomorphic inverse-square-root operation respects conjugation/swap symmetry, so the pure same-point sector is invariant under exchanging the two points. Thus it is invariant under \(s\mapsto -s\), i.e. it is an even function of \(s\). The working notes already use exactly this swap-symmetry mechanism for the corrected local block and for the odd-germ construction. turn121file1turn121file2

By definition, the odd two-point germ is obtained by projecting to the odd part under \(s\mapsto -s\). Therefore every even contribution vanishes in that projection. Hence the entire pure same-point septic sector dies already before fixed-sector projection or quotient normalization. This gives
\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}=0
\]
in the odd germ, and therefore also
\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0.
\]
\(\square\)

---

That is the full odd-germ upgrade of the current weight-one statement. The existing weight-one lemma/corollary only used two ingredients:

1. odd-germ means odd part under \(s\mapsto -s\), and  
2. pure same-point terms are invariant under \(t_+\leftrightarrow t_-\).

Neither ingredient depends on the \(q^{(7)}\)-weight bookkeeping. So the same proof works for the full pure same-point septic sector, not just \([\Delta_7]^{[1]}\). turn121file12

Once you combine this with the already-derived \(K_5\) shadow formula
\[
A_{7,K_5}=c_2A_5+[B_2,A_5]
\]
and the projected septic gauge law
\[
(A_7^{\mathfrak f})^{\new}=A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
you get:

- \(A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\),
- \(A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0\),
- and the only remaining quotient-level order-\(7\) issue is the \(K_3\)-sector. The exact septic law already strongly suggests that \(K_3\) is the order-\(4\) shadow and has zero fixed projection as well, since all order-\(4\) shadow terms in the septic gauge law are anti-fixed. turn112file10turn109file15

So the remaining math gap is now extremely small. After formalizing the pure same-point parity lemma at the full odd-germ level, the next exact target is just:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\quad\text{(or at least }[A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}]=0\text{ in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{).}
}
\]

That is the last serious quotient-septic lemma.

\[
A_7^{\new}

+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
